
============== high level task decomposition ================
[{'objective': 'Rewrite the polynomial equation in a symmetric or factorized form to simplify the constraint.'}, {'objective': 'Use the constraint a + b + c = 300 to express one variable in terms of the others and substitute into the simplified polynomial.'}, {'objective': 'Solve the resulting equation(s) over nonnegative integers (a,b,c) satisfying the sum constraint.'}, {'objective': 'Count the number of valid triples (a,b,c) that satisfy both the sum and polynomial equation.'}]
============== task analysis ================
1. Extract and Summarize Given Information:
- Variables: Nonnegative integers a, b, c.
- Constraints:
  - Linear: a + b + c = 300.
  - Nonlinear: a^2b + a^2c + b^2a + b^2c + c^2a + c^2b = 6,000,000.
- Objective: Find the number of triples (a,b,c) satisfying both conditions.

2. Analyze Relationships Between Components:
- The first condition restricts the sum of the variables to a fixed total.
- The second condition is symmetric in a, b, c and involves terms of the form a^2b and a^2c, which can be grouped or rewritten to reveal underlying algebraic structure.
- The nonlinear sum can be expressed as a sum over permutations of squared and linear terms, indicating symmetry and potential factorization.
- The constraints together define a discrete set of points on a plane (or lattice points in 3D) intersecting a nonlinear surface.
- The problem likely requires exploiting symmetry and algebraic manipulation to reduce complexity.

3. Identify the Field of Study:
- Primary domain: Combinatorics (counting integer solutions).
- Secondary domains: Algebra (polynomial identities, symmetric sums), Number Theory (integer solutions), possibly Discrete Mathematics.
- Contexts: Problems of this type appear in mathematical competitions, integer partition theory, and algebraic combinatorics.

4. Highlight Aspects Needing Clarification:
- The problem is well-defined but challenging due to the nonlinear constraint.
- Potential ambiguity in whether permutations of (a,b,c) count as distinct solutions or not; presumably all ordered triples count.
- The complexity of the nonlinear equation suggests that direct enumeration is impractical.
- Assumptions: Treat (a,b,c) as ordered triples; all variables are integers ≥ 0; no further constraints.
- The problem may require recognizing or deriving an equivalent, simpler form of the nonlinear sum to proceed.

async def forward(self, taskInfo):
    from collections import Counter
    print("Task Requirement: ", taskInfo)
    sub_tasks = []
    agents = []
    logs = []

    cot_instruction_1 = "Sub-task 1: Identify and clearly state the domain of the problem: all ordered triples (a,b,c) of nonnegative integers such that a + b + c = 300, with context from the user query."
    cot_agent_1 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)

        "subtask_id": "subtask_1",
        "instruction": cot_instruction_1,
        "context": ["user query"],
        "agent_collaboration": "CoT"
    }

    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 1 output: thinking - {thinking1.content}; answer - {answer1.content}")
    subtask_desc_1['response'] = {"thinking": thinking1, "answer": answer1}
    logs.append(subtask_desc_1)

    N_sc = self.max_sc
    cot_agents_2 = [LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.5) for _ in range(N_sc)]
    possible_answers_2 = []

        "subtask_id": "subtask_2",
        "instruction": cot_sc_instruction_2,

        possible_answers_2.append(answer2)

    thinking2, answer2 = await final_decision_agent_2([taskInfo] + possible_answers_2 + possible_thinkings_2, "Sub-task 2: Synthesize and choose the most consistent algebraic simplification for the nonlinear constraint.", is_sub_task=True)

async def forward(self, taskInfo):
    from collections import Counter
    print("Task Requirement: ", taskInfo)
    sub_tasks = []
    agents = []
    logs = []

    # Stage 0: Domain Identification and Initial Analysis

    cot_instruction_1 = (
        "Sub-task 1: Identify and clearly state the domain of the problem: all ordered triples (a,b,c) "
        "of nonnegative integers such that a + b + c = 300. Emphasize the nonnegativity and ordering of variables without attempting to solve any constraints."
    )
    cot_agent_1 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)

        "subtask_id": "subtask_1",
        "instruction": cot_instruction_1,
        "context": ["user query"],
        "agent_collaboration": "CoT"
    }

    agents.append(f"CoT agent {cot_agent_1.id}, identifying domain, thinking: {thinking1.content}; answer: {answer1.content}")
    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 1 output: thinking - {thinking1.content}; answer - {answer1.content}")
    subtask_desc1['response'] = {"thinking": thinking1, "answer": answer1}
    logs.append(subtask_desc1)

    cot_sc_instruction_2 = (

    possible_answers_2 = []

This theorem states that the number of nonnegative integer solutions to x_1 + x_2 + ... + x_k = n is given by C(n + k - 1, k - 1), where C denotes the binomial coefficient. Here, k = 3 and n = 300.
